This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n    21→//\n    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n    29→//\n    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n    33→// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n    34→// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n    35→// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n    36→// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n    37→//\n    38→// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n    39→// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n    40→// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n    41→// availability.\n    42→//\n    43→// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n    44→// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n    45→// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n    46→// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n    47→// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n    48→// to master availability.\n    49→//\n    50→// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n    51→// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n    52→// your own risk.\n    53→package leaderelection\n    54→\n    55→import (\n    56→\t\"bytes\"\n    57→\t\"context\"\n    58→\t\"fmt\"\n    59→\t\"sync\"\n    60→\t\"time\"\n    61→\n    62→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n    63→\tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n    64→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n    65→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n    66→\trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n    67→\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n    68→\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n    69→)\n    70→\n    71→const (\n    72→\tJitterFactor = 1.2\n    73→)\n    74→\n    75→// NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n    76→func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n    77→\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n    78→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n    79→\t}\n    80→\tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n    81→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n    82→\t}\n    83→\tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n    84→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n    85→\t}\n    86→\tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n    87→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n    88→\t}\n    89→\tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n    90→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n    91→\t}\n    92→\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\n    93→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n    94→\t}\n    95→\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n    96→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n    97→\t}\n    98→\n    99→\tif lec.Lock == nil {\n   100→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n//\n// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n//\n// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n// availability.\n//\n// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n// to master availability.\n//\n// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. lease-based leader election mechanism that relies on the Kubernetes API server and Lease objects in the coordination API. This is implemented in `k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **LeaderElector** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go): The main client-side component that orchestrates leader election\\n   - `Run()`: Starts the election loop, calling `acquire()` to get leadership, then `renew()` to maintain it\\n   - `acquire(ctx)`: Loops attempting to acquire the lease through `tryAcquireOrRenew()` with RetryPeriod delays\\n   - `renew(ctx)`: Continuously renews the lease with a RenewDeadline timeout; if renewal fails, stops leading\\n   - `tryAcquireOrRenew()`: Core logic that checks if the lease is valid and updates the Lease object\\n\\n2. **ResourceLock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go): Abstraction for different lock backends\\n   - `Interface` defines Get(), Create(), Update() operations\\n   - `LeaderElectionRecord` contains: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n\\n3. **LeaseLock** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): Implements the Interface using Kubernetes Lease API\\n   - Uses `coordinationv1.Lease` objects stored in etcd\\n   - `Get()`: Retrieves the current lease from the API server\\n   - `Update()`: Updates the RenewTime and holder identity in the lease spec\\n\\n4. **LeaseCandidate** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leasecandidate.go): Advanced coordinated leader election using LeaseCandidate objects for version-based leader selection\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Timeout-based detection**: Leaders continuously renew their lease before RenewDeadline expires\\n- **LeaseDuration**: Non-leaders must wait for this duration without observing an update before attempting to acquire\\n- **Leader transitions**: When a leader can't renew before RenewDeadline, the lease becomes stale\\n- **Acquisition**: Any non-leader can then update the lease and become the new leader\\n- **Re-election**: Tracked via LeaderTransitions counter; leader change triggers OnNewLeader callbacks\\n- **Integration** (pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/leaderelection_controller.go): Kubernetes control plane components use this for HA setup\\n\\n---\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for distributed leader election, implemented in the go.etcd.io/raft/v3 library. The server integration is in `server/etcdserver`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Wrapper around the Raft state machine\\n   - `start(rh *raftReadyHandler)`: Launches the raft node's event loop\\n   - Processes `raft.Ready()` messages containing RaftState changes\\n   - Detects leader changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead` (peer ID of current leader)\\n   - Metrics: leaderChanges counter, hasLeader flag, isLeader flag track leadership transitions\\n\\n2. **raftReadyHandler** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Interface for raft state machine to notify EtcdServer\\n   - `getLead()`: Returns current leader ID from atomic variable\\n   - `updateLead(lead uint64)`: Sets the leader ID when Raft reports a change\\n   - `updateLeadership(newLeader bool)`: Called when leadership status changes\\n\\n3. **EtcdServer** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Integrates Raft with the etcd server\\n   - `lead` (atomic.Uint64): Atomic variable storing the current leader's member ID\\n   - `leaderChanged`: Notifier channel that broadcasts when leader changes\\n   - `isLeader()`: Checks if `MemberID() == Lead()`\\n   - `Leader()`: Returns current leader as types.ID\\n   - `LeaderChangedNotify()`: Returns channel for monitoring leadership changes\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Heartbeat detection**: Leader sends periodic heartbeat messages to followers\\n- **Election trigger**: When followers don't receive heartbeats within an election timeout, they become candidates\\n- **Raft election**: Candidates request votes from other peers; first to get majority becomes leader\\n- **State machine update**: When Raft detects a new leader (rd.SoftState.Lead != previous), it calls `updateLeadership(newLeader=true)`\\n- **Notification**: `leaderChanged.Notify()` broadcasts to all listeners (e.g., linearizable read handlers)\\n- **Leadership actions** (updateLeadership callback):\\n  - On becoming leader: Record election time (`leadElectedTime`), resume compactor\\n  - On losing leadership: Pause compactor, demote lessor\\n  - Logs leadership status to stats\\n- **Consensus guarantee**: Raft ensures only one leader per term, preventing split-brain scenarios\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes (Lease-Based) | etcd (Raft-Based) |\\n|--------|--------------------------|-------------------|\\n| **Election Mechanism** | Optimistic concurrency control via API server updates | Consensus algorithm with voting |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Timeout-based (LeaseDuration) | Heartbeat timeout + election |\\n| **Implementation** | Client-side, decoupled from data layer | Integrated with consensus for consistency |\\n| **Consistency** | Best-effort, clock-dependent | Strong, term-based ordering |\\n| **State Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API objects | Raft state machine, persistent log |\\n| **Notification** | LeaderCallbacks (OnStartedLeading, OnStoppedLeading) | leaderChanged channel, LeaderChangedNotify() |\\n| **Guarantee** | No fencing; two leaders possible during clock skew | No split-brain; Raft consensus prevents dual leaders |\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2866,"cache_read_input_tokens":53511,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2866},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ef2cf96d-8db4-4770-9923-d02f3f1e7ffd","uuid":"d2448566-4973-4df8-9b55-c8f918ec8e7b"}

The server integration is in `server/etcdserver`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Wrapper around the Raft state machine\\n   - `start(rh *raftReadyHandler)`: Launches the raft node's event loop\\n   - Processes `raft.Ready()` messages containing RaftState changes\\n   - Detects leader changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead` (peer ID of current leader)\\n   - Metrics: leaderChanges counter, hasLeader flag, isLeader flag track leadership transitions\\n\\n2. **raftReadyHandler** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Interface for raft state machine to notify EtcdServer\\n   - `getLead()`: Returns current leader ID from atomic variable\\n   - `updateLead(lead uint64)`: Sets the leader ID when Raft reports a change\\n   - `updateLeadership(newLeader bool)`: Called when leadership status changes\\n\\n3. **EtcdServer** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Integrates Raft with the etcd server\\n   - `lead` (atomic.Uint64): Atomic variable storing the current leader's member ID\\n   - `leaderChanged`: Notifier channel that broadcasts when leader changes\\n   - `isLeader()`: Checks if `MemberID() == Lead()`\\n   - `Leader()`: Returns current leader as types.ID\\n   - `LeaderChangedNotify()`: Returns channel for monitoring leadership changes\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Heartbeat detection**: Leader sends periodic heartbeat messages to followers\\n- **Election trigger**: When followers don't receive heartbeats within an election timeout, they become candidates\\n- **Raft election**: Candidates request votes from other peers; first to get majority becomes leader\\n- **State machine update**: When Raft detects a new leader (rd.SoftState.Lead != previous), it calls `updateLeadership(newLeader=true)`\\n- **Notification**: `leaderChanged.Notify()` broadcasts to all listeners (e.g., linearizable read handlers)\\n- **Leadership actions** (updateLeadership callback):\\n  - On becoming leader: Record election time (`leadElectedTime`), resume compactor\\n  - On losing leadership: Pause compactor, demote lessor\\n  - Logs leadership status to stats\\n- **Consensus guarantee**: Raft ensures only one leader per term, preventing split-brain scenarios\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes (Lease-Based) | etcd (Raft-Based) |\\n|--------|--------------------------|-------------------|\\n| **Election Mechanism** | Optimistic concurrency control via API server updates | Consensus algorithm with voting |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Timeout-based (LeaseDuration) | Heartbeat timeout + election |\\n| **Implementation** | Client-side, decoupled from data layer | Integrated with consensus for consistency |\\n| **Consistency** | Best-effort, clock-dependent | Strong, term-based ordering |\\n| **State Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API objects | Raft state machine, persistent log |\\n| **Notification** | LeaderCallbacks (OnStartedLeading, OnStoppedLeading) | leaderChanged channel, LeaderChangedNotify() |\\n| **Guarantee** | No fencing; two leaders possible during clock skew | No split-brain; Raft consensus prevents dual leaders |\\n\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

The server integration is in `server/etcdserver`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Wrapper around the Raft state machine\\n   - `start(rh *raftReadyHandler)`: Launches the raft node's event loop\\n   - Processes `raft.Ready()` messages containing RaftState changes\\n   - Detects leader changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead` (peer ID of current leader)\\n   - Metrics: leaderChanges counter, hasLeader flag, isLeader flag track leadership transitions\\n\\n2. **raftReadyHandler** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Interface for raft state machine to notify EtcdServer\\n   - `getLead()`: Returns current leader ID from atomic variable\\n   - `updateLead(lead uint64)`: Sets the leader ID when Raft reports a change\\n   - `updateLeadership(newLeader bool)`: Called when leadership status changes\\n\\n3. **EtcdServer** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Integrates Raft with the etcd server\\n   - `lead` (atomic.Uint64): Atomic variable storing the current leader's member ID\\n   - `leaderChanged`: Notifier channel that broadcasts when leader changes\\n   - `isLeader()`: Checks if `MemberID() == Lead()`\\n   - `Leader()`: Returns current leader as types.ID\\n   - `LeaderChangedNotify()`: Returns channel for monitoring leadership changes\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Heartbeat detection**: Leader sends periodic heartbeat messages to followers\\n- **Election trigger**: When followers don't receive heartbeats within an election timeout, they become candidates\\n- **Raft election**: Candidates request votes from other peers; first to get majority becomes leader\\n- **State machine update**: When Raft detects a new leader (rd.SoftState.Lead != previous), it calls `updateLeadership(newLeader=true)`\\n- **Notification**: `leaderChanged.Notify()` broadcasts to all listeners (e.g., linearizable read handlers)\\n- **Leadership actions** (updateLeadership callback):\\n  - On becoming leader: Record election time (`leadElectedTime`), resume compactor\\n  - On losing leadership: Pause compactor, demote lessor\\n  - Logs leadership status to stats\\n- **Consensus guarantee**: Raft ensures only one leader per term, preventing split-brain scenarios\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes (Lease-Based) | etcd (Raft-Based) |\\n|--------|--------------------------|-------------------|\\n| **Election Mechanism** | Optimistic concurrency control via API server updates | Consensus algorithm with voting |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Timeout-based (LeaseDuration) | Heartbeat timeout + election |\\n| **Implementation** | Client-side, decoupled from data layer | Integrated with consensus for consistency |\\n| **Consistency** | Best-effort, clock-dependent | Strong, term-based ordering |\\n| **State Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API objects | Raft state machine, persistent log |\\n| **Notification** | LeaderCallbacks (OnStartedLeading, OnStoppedLeading) | leaderChanged channel, LeaderChangedNotify() |\\n| **Guarantee** | No fencing; two leaders possible during clock skew | No split-brain; Raft consensus prevents dual leaders |\\n\"\n}\n---\n175 /workspace/answer.json","stderr":"","interrupted":false,"isImage":false,"noOutputExpected":false}}
